class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-111"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-111">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Spelt <i>ng</i>, always <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/\xc5\x8b/</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-113"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-113">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/t/</span> may be a glottal stop between vowels or word final.<sup id="cite_ref-Johnston,_Paul_1997_p.501_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Johnston,_Paul_1997_p.501-112">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> In Ulster dentalised pronunciations may also occur, also for <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/d/</span>.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-114"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-114">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In Northern dialects the clusters <i>kn</i> and <i>gn</i> may be realised as <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/kn/</span>, <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/tn/</span> and <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/\xc9\xa1n/</span><sup id="cite_ref-Johnston,_Paul_1997_p.501_112-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Johnston,_Paul_1997_p.501-112">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> e.g. <i>knap</i> (talk), <i>knee</i>, <i>knowe</i> (knoll), etc.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-116"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-116">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The cluster <i>nch</i> is usually realised <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/n\xca\x83/</span><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> e.g. <i>brainch</i> (branch), <i>dunch</i> (push), etc.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-119"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-119">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Spelt <i>th</i>. In Mid Northern varieties an intervocallic <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/\xc3\xb0/</span> may be realised <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/d/</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> Initial \'th\' in <i>thing</i>, <i>think</i> and <i>thank</i>, etc. may be <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/h/</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-Johnston,_Paul_1997_p.507_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Johnston,_Paul_1997_p.507-118">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-120"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-120">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Both <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/s/</span> and <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/z/</span> may be spelt <i>s</i> or <i>se</i>. <i>Z</i> is seldom used for <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/z/</span> but may occur in some words as a substitute for the older &#x27e8;<i lang="ang" title="Old English language text">\xc8\x9d</i>&#x27e9; (<a href="/wiki/Yogh" title="Yogh">yogh</a>) realised <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/j\xc9\xaa/</span> or <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/\xc5\x8b/</span>. For example: <i>brulzie</i> (broil), <i>gaberlunzie</i> (a beggar) and the names <i><a href="/wiki/Menzies" title="Menzies">Menzies</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Finzean" title="Finzean">Finzean</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Culzean" class="mw-redirect" title="Culzean">Culzean</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Mackenzie_(surname)" title="Mackenzie (surname)">Mackenzie</a></i> etc.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-ch-122"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-ch_122-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-ch_122-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Spelt <i>ch</i>, also <i>gh</i>. Medial \'cht\' may be <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/\xc3\xb0/</span> in Northern dialects. <i>loch</i> (fjord or lake), <i>nicht</i> (night), <i>dochter</i> (daughter), <i>dreich</i> (dreary), etc. Similar to the German "Na<i>ch</i>t".<sup id="cite_ref-Johnston,_Paul_1997_p.499_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Johnston,_Paul_1997_p.499-121">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> The spelling <i>ch</i> is realised <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/t\xca\x83/</span> word initially or where it follows \'r\' e.g. <i>airch</i> (arch), <i>mairch</i> (march), etc.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-r-124"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-r_124-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-r_124-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Spelt <i>r</i> and pronounced in all positions,<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> i.e. <a href="/wiki/Rhotic_consonant" title="Rhotic consonant">rhotically</a>.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-125"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-125">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><i>W</i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/w/</span> and <i>wh</i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/\xca\x8d/</span>, older <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/x\xca\x8d/</span>, do not merge.<sup id="cite_ref-Johnston,_Paul_1997_p.499_121-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Johnston,_Paul_1997_p.499-121">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> Northern dialects also have <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/f/</span> for <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/\xca\x8d/</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-Johnston,_Paul_1997_p.507_118-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Johnston,_Paul_1997_p.507-118">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> The cluster <i>wr</i> may be realised <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/wr/</span>, more often <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/r/</span>, but may be <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/vr/</span> in Northern dialects<sup id="cite_ref-Johnston,_Paul_1997_p.507_118-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Johnston,_Paul_1997_p.507-118">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> e.g. <i>wrack</i> (wreck), <i>wrang</i> (wrong), <i>write</i>, <i>wrocht</i> (worked), etc.</span>\n</li>\n</ol></div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a
